كتاب الطهارة
الأنف والبنصر والوسطى والسبابة فوقه واجعل الإبهام أسفل رأسه تحته كما وراه ابن مسعود، ولا يقبض القبضة على السواك فإن ذلك يورث الباسور، ويبدأ بالأسنان العليا من الجانب الأيمن ثم الأيسر ثم السفلى كذلك، كذا في شرح منية المصلي، وتقوم الأصبع أو الخرقة الخشنة مقامه عند فقده أو عدم أسنانه في تحصيل الثواب لا عند وجوده .. والأفضل أن يبدأ بالسبابة اليسرى ثم باليمنى، والعلك يقوم مقامه للمرأة لكون المواظبة عليه تضعف أسنانها فيستحب لها فعله، ومنافعه كثيرة منها أنه يرضي الرب ويسخط الشيطان ومن خشي من السواك القيء تركه . ويكره أن يستاك مضطجعاً فإنه يورث كبر الطحال. كذا في السراج الوهاج.
Book of Purity. The nose, the ring finger, the middle, and the index finger above it, and place the thumb below its head under it, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. And do not grip the miswak with a fist, for that causes hemorrhoids. And begin with the upper teeth from the right side, then the left, then the lower similarly, as in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And the finger or a rough cloth takes its place when it is absent or when one has no teeth, in obtaining reward, not when it is present. And the better is to begin with the left index finger then the right. And gum takes its place for a woman because using it continuously weakens her teeth, so it is recommended for her to use it. And its benefits are many: it pleases the Lord, enrages Satan, and if one fears vomiting from siwak, he abandons it. And it is disliked to use siwak while lying down, for it causes enlargement of the spleen. As in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the recommended etiquettes of using the siwak. The author begins by describing the proper grip: the little finger (likely meant), ring finger, middle, and index finger are placed above the siwak, with the thumb below the head, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud. Gripping the siwak with a fist is discouraged as it causes hemorrhoids. One should start with the upper teeth on the right side, then the left, then the lower teeth similarly. If siwak is unavailable or one has no teeth, a finger or rough cloth can substitute to attain reward, but not when siwak is present. It is better to start with the left index finger then the right. For women, gum is recommended as a substitute because frequent use of siwak weakens their teeth. The benefits are numerous: pleasing Allah, enraging Satan, and if one fears vomiting, he should abandon it. Using siwak while lying down is makruh as it enlarges the spleen. All these rulings are based on hadith and statements of early scholars.

Key Terms
السواك (al-siwaak): The toothstick used for cleaning the teeth; a Sunnah act.
مكروه (makruuh): Disliked; an act whose abandonment is rewarded but performance is not sinful.
الأنف (al-anf): In the OCR, likely a corruption of 'الخنصر' (little finger).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is makruh when using siwak?
A) Using it while standing
B) Using it while lying down
C) Using it before prayer
D) Using it after waking

Key Takeaway
Siwak is a confirmed Sunnah with specific etiquettes; using it lying down is makruh, and substitutes are valid only when siwak is unavailable.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Madmadah and Istinshaq: Confirmed Sunnahs in Wudu and Ghusl
Definition and ruling of madmadah and istinshaq with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of madmadah and istinshaq in the Hanafi school, explain their performance, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position regarding the use of new water.

Core Idea
Madmadah and istinshaq are confirmed sunnahs—leaving them without excuse is sinful, yet they are not fard.

In wudu and ghusl, rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and sniffing water into the nose (istinshaq) are highly emphasized practices. This lesson unpacks their legal status, definitions, and the details of proper performance, including a key inter-madhhab dispute about whether to use fresh water for each act and each repetition. We will follow the Hanafi position as established in the authoritative texts.

Guided Path
1
Define the Acts
Identify the linguistic and terminological meanings of madmadah (rinsing the entire mouth) and istinshaq (delivering water to the soft part of the nose).
These definitions distinguish them from mere washing.
2
Identify the Ruling and Its Evidence
Note that both are sunnah mu'akkadah. The proof is the hadith commanding mubalaghah (exaggeration) except for a fasting person, and the continuous practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and the Companions.
The ruling is based on zahir al-riwayah.
3
Understand Mubalaghah
For madmadah, mubalaghah is achieved by gargling (ghargara); for istinshaq, by istinthar (expelling water). Also, swallowing water during madmadah suffices but expelling is better because the water becomes musta'mal (used).
4
Examine the Dispute on Water Usage
Hanafis hold that new water must be taken for each madmadah and for each istinshaq, and for each repetition (tathlith). Shafi'is consider one cup sufficient for all. The Hanafi proof is the hadith of al-Tabarani where the Prophet took new water each time.
Abu Dawud's silence on this hadith indicates it is hasan according to al-Nawawi.
5
Apply the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi. Thus, in practice, one should use separate water for madmadah and istinshaq and renew water for each of the three repetitions.

قوله ( وغسل فمه وأنفه عدل عن المضمضة والاستنشاق المذكورين في أصله الوافي للاختصار، وما في الشرح من أن الغسل يشعر بالاستيعاب فكان أولى فيه نظر، فإن المضمضة كذلك فإنها اصطلاحاً استيعاب الماء جميع الفم كما في الخلاصة، وفي اللغة التحريك والاستنشاق لغة من النشق وهو جذب الماء ونحوه بريح الأنف إلى داخله، واصطلاحاً إيصال الماء إلى مارن الأنف. كذا في الخلاصة والمارن مالان من والمبالغة سنة فيهما أيضاً كذا في الوافي لحديث أصحاب السنن الأربعة «بالغ في المضمضة والاستنشاق إلا أن تكون صائماً» (١) وهي في المضمضة بالغرغرة وفي الاستنشاق بالاستنثار كذا في الكافي والاستنثاء دفع الماء ونحوه للخروج من الأنف، وقد وافقه في فتح القدير على الأول. وقال في الثاني كما في الخلاصة إلى ما اشتدّ من الأنف. وفي الخلاصة : هي في المضمضة أن يصل إلى رأس الحلق. وقال شمس الأئمة هي في المضمضة أن يدير الماء في فيه من جانب إلى جانب، والأولى ما في فتح القدير ذكره بعضهم. ولو تمضمض وابتلع أجزأه لأن المج ليس من حقيقتها، والأفضل أن يلقيه لأنه ماء مستعمل. وفي الظهيرية وإذا أخذ الماء بكفه فمضمض ببعضه واستنشق بالباقي جاز وبخلاف ذلك لا يجوز وفي المجتبى : لو رفع الماء من كف واحدة للمضمضة جاز وللاستنشاق لا يجوز ينافي ذلك كما لا ينافي استحبابه عند غيره مما مر على أنه يبعد استحبابه في الصلاة التي هي مناجاة للرب تعالى سيما عند بعد العهد من الوضوء مع ما فيها من قراءة القرآن التي يستحب استعماله عندها وحضور الملائكة عندها مع أنهم استحبوه عند مجامع الناس، فبالأولى مع الملائكة . قال في هدية ابن العماد روى جابر رضي الله تعالى عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «إذا قام أحدكم يصلي من الليل فليستك فإن أحدكم إذا قرأ في صلاته وضع ملك فاه على فيه لا يخرج من فيه شيء إلا دخل فم الملك أسنده البيهقي في شعب الإيمان .اهـ. قوله: (وبخلاف ذلك لا يجوز)

كتاب الطهارة
لصيرورة الماء مستعملاً، ولا يخفى أن نفي الجواز في المسألتين بمعنى نفي الإجزاء في تحصيل السنة لا بمعنى الحرمة لما أن أصلهما سنة، أو تحمل على المضمضة والاستنشاق في الغسل الواجب وقالوا المضمضة والاستنشاق سنتان مشتملتان على سنن منها تقديم المضمضة على الاستنشاق بالإجماع، ومنها التثليث في حق كل واحد بالإجماع، وأخذ ماء جديد في التثليث سنة عندنا وعند الشافعي بماء واحد، وأخذ ماء جديد لكل واحد منهما سنة عندنا، وعند الشافعي لهما ماء واحد وإزالة المخاط باليد اليسرى. كذا في المعراج. وفي البدائع والمبسوط : وفعلهما باليمين سنة. وفي المنية أنه يستنشق باليسرى وفي المعراج : ترك التكرار لا يكره مع الإمكان. قال أستاذنا يتبين من هذا أن من عنده ماء يكفي للغسل مرة مع المضمضة والاستنشاق أو ثلاثاً بدونهما يغسل مرة معهما. وفي السراج: إنهما سنتان مؤكدتان، فإن ترك المضمضة والاستنشاق أثم على الصحيح ا هـ . ولا يخفى أن الإثم منوط بترك الواجب، ويمكن الجواب مما قالوه من أن السنة المؤكدة في قوة الواجب ودليل سنيتهما المواظبة كما في الهداية. وفي غاية البيان يعني مع الترك أحياناً وإلا كانتا واجبتين. وقد علمت مما قدمناه أن المواظبة من غير ترك لا تفيد الوجوب وجميع من حكى وضوءه عليه السلام اثنان وعشرون صحابياً كلهم ذكروهما فيه كما في فتح القدير. وفي نسخة شرح عليها مسكين غسل فمه وأنفه بمياه وقال : قوله بمياه متعلق بكل واحد والذي في الوافي غسل فمه بمياه وأنفه بمياه وهو أولى مما في الكنز ليدل على تجديد الماء في كل منهما، وقد جاء مصرحاً به في حديث الطبراني من قوله فمضمض ثلاثاً واستنشق ثلاثاً يأخذ لكل مرة ماء جديداً ورواه أبو داود وسكت فكان حجة . وما ورد مما ظاهره المخالفة فمحمول على الموافقة كما في فتح القدير. وفي السراج الوهاج : ولو تمضمض ثلاثاً من غرفة واحدة لم يصر آتياً أي بأن استنشق ببعضه وتمضمض بالباقي . قوله : (قال أستاذنا يتبين من هذا الخ) هو من كلام المعراج . ثم أن الإشارة في قوله من هذا لا يظهر رجوعها إلى قوله ترك التكرار لا يكره أي تكرار المضمضة والاستنشاق كما لا يخفى، بل هو راجع إلى كونهما سنتين مؤكدتين بأثم بتركهما . وعبارة المعراج نصها هكذا : وفي الشفاء المضمضمة والاستنشاق سنتان مؤكدتان من تركهما يأثم. وفي مبسوط شيخ الإسلام ترك التكرار لا يكره مع الإمكان. قال أستاذنا : يتبين من هذا الخ. قوله: (يغسل مرة معهما) أي لأن النبي ورد عنه ترك التثليث حيث غسل مرة مرة وقال : «هذا وضوء لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا به ولم يرد عنه ترك المضمضة والاستنشاق كما سيأتي . قوله : ورواه أبو داود وسكت عنه) قال الإمام النووي في مختصره المسمى بالتقريب : ومن مظانه أي الحسن سنن أبي داود فقد جاء عنه أنه يذكر فيه الصحيح وما يشبهه ويقاربه وما كان فيه وهن شديد بينه وما لم يذكر فيه شيئاً فهو صالح فعلى هذا ما وجدنا في كتابه مطلقاً ولم يصححه غيره من المعتمدين ولا ضعفه فهو حسن عند أبي داود اهـ.
His statement (and washing his mouth and nose): He turned away from the madmadah and istinshaq mentioned in his original work al-Wafi for brevity. And what is in the sharh that washing implies thoroughness so it was better is subject to consideration, because madmadah is the same, for terminologically it is the thoroughness of water in the entire mouth as in al-Khulasa, and linguistically it is movement. And istinshaq linguistically is from nashq, which is drawing water etc. with the breath of the nose into its interior, and terminologically it is delivering water to the soft part of the nose. As in al-Khulasa, and the soft part is what is soft. And mubalaghah is sunnah in both as well, as in al-Wafi, due to the hadith of the authors of the four Sunan: 'Exaggerate in madmadah and istinshaq unless you are fasting.' (1) And it is in madmadah by gargling, and in istinshaq by istinthar, as in al-Kafi. And istinthar is pushing water etc. out of the nose. And he agreed with him in Fath al-Qadir on the first. And he said regarding the second, as in al-Khulasa, to the point where the nose becomes intense. And in al-Khulasa: It is in madmadah that the water reaches the top of the throat. And Shams al-A'imma said she in madmadah that she circulates water in her mouth from side to side, and the better is what is in Fath al-Qadir, some mentioned it. And if he performs madmadah and swallows, it suffices him because rinsing is not part of its reality, and it is better that he expectorates it because it is used water. And in al-Zahiriyya: If he takes water in his hand and performs madmadah with some and istinshaq with the rest, it is permissible, and otherwise it is not permissible. And in al-Mujtaba: If he lifts water from one handful for madmadah, it is permissible, and for istinshaq it is not permissible, that contradicts just as it does not contradict its recommendation by others, from what has passed, that it is far from being recommended in prayer which is private conversation with the Lord, especially when there is a long interval from wudu, along with what is in it of reciting Qur'an for which it is recommended to use it, and the presence of angels, while they recommended it at gatherings of people, so it is more appropriate with angels. He said in Hadiyyat Ibn al-'Imad: Jabir reported that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'When one of you stands to pray at night, let him use the siwak, for when one of you recites in his prayer, an angel places his mouth on his mouth; nothing comes out of his mouth but enters the mouth of the angel.' Al-Bayhaqi related it in Shu'ab al-Iman. End. His statement: (And otherwise it is not permissible). Water. And he did not expectorate it. Absence. Presence. (1) Reported by al-Tirmidhi in Book of Fasting, chapter 68; Abu Dawud in Book of Purity, chapter 56; al-Nasa'i in Book of Purity, chapter 70; Ahmad in his Musnad (4/33). Book of Purity. Because the water becomes used. And it is not hidden that the negation of permissibility in the two issues means negation of adequacy in obtaining the sunnah, not in the sense of prohibition, because their origin is sunnah, or it is interpreted as madmadah and istinshaq in obligatory ghusl. And they said: Madmadah and istinshaq are two sunnahs that include sunnahs: among them is giving precedence to madmadah over istinshaq by consensus, and among them is thuluth (doing three times) for each one by consensus, and taking new water for thuluth is sunnah in our school, while according to al-Shafi'i it is with one water, and taking new water for each of them is sunnah in our school, while according to al-Shafi'i they have one water, and removing mucus with the left hand. As in al-Mi'raj. And in al-Bada'i' and al-Mabsut: Doing them with the right is sunnah. And in al-Munya: That he does istinshaq with the left. And in al-Mi'raj: Abandoning repetition is not disliked when possible. Our teacher said: From this it becomes clear that whoever has water sufficient for ghusl once with madmadah and istinshaq or three times without them, he should wash once with them. And in al-Siraj: They are two confirmed sunnahs, so if one abandons madmadah and istinshaq, he sins according to the correct opinion. End. And it is not hidden that sin is contingent on abandoning an obligation, and it is possible to answer what they said that the confirmed sunnah is like an obligation, and the evidence for their being sunnah is continuous practice as in al-Hidaya. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: meaning with occasional abandonment, otherwise they would be obligatory. And you have known from what we have presented that continuous practice without abandonment does not necessitate obligation, and all who related his wudu, peace be upon him, twenty-two companions, all mentioned them in it, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in a copy of a commentary by Miskin: 'He washed his mouth and nose with waters,' and he said: His statement 'with waters' is attached to each one, and that which is in al-Wafi is 'He washed his mouth with waters and his nose with waters', and it is better than what is in al-Kanz to indicate renewing water in each of them. And it has come explicitly in the hadith of al-Tabarani from his statement: 'He performed madmadah three times and istinshaq three times, taking new water for each time.' And Abu Dawud reported it and remained silent, so it was a proof. And what has been reported that apparently contradicts is interpreted as agreeing, as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: And if he performs madmadah three times from one cup, it is not considered as doing it, i.e., by performing istinshaq with some and madmadah with the rest. His statement: (Our teacher said: from this it becomes clear etc.) is from the speech of al-Mi'raj. Then, the reference in his words 'from this' does not appear to refer to his words 'abandoning repetition is not disliked', i.e., repeating madmadah and istinshaq, as is not hidden, but rather it refers to their being two confirmed sunnahs with sin for abandoning them. And the wording of al-Mi'raj is as follows: And in al-Shifa': Madmadah and istinshaq are two confirmed sunnahs; whoever abandons them sins. And in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam: Abandoning repetition is not disliked when possible. Our teacher said: From this it becomes clear etc. His statement: (He washes once with them) meaning because the Prophet, peace be upon him, is reported to have abandoned thuluth, as he washed once and said: 'This is a wudu without which Allah does not accept prayer,' and he did not report abandoning madmadah and istinshaq, as will come. His statement: (And Abu Dawud reported it and remained silent about it). Imam al-Nawawi said in his abridgment called al-Taqrib: And among its places, i.e., hasan, is Sunan Abi Dawud, for it has come from him that he mentions in it the authentic and what resembles it and what is close to it, and what has severe weakness, and what he does not mention anything about, then it is sound. So according to this, what we find in his book absolutely and no one from the reliable scholars authenticated it nor weakened it, then it is hasan according to Abu Dawud. End.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides a comprehensive discussion of madmadah (rinsing the mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into the nose) in wudu and ghusl. The author begins by explaining the terminology: madmadah linguistically means movement, but terminologically it is the thorough rinsing of the entire mouth. Istinshaq is drawing water into the nose, reaching the soft part. Both acts are sunnah, and mubalaghah (exaggeration) is recommended except for a fasting person. The hadith from the four Sunan is cited as proof. Different definitions of mubalaghah are given: in madmadah it is gargling, in istinshaq it is istinthar (expelling water). There is a discussion on whether swallowing water during madmadah suffices; it does, but spitting it out is better because it becomes used water. The author then addresses the issue of taking water from one handful for both acts: it is permissible only if done in a specific order (madmadah then istinshaq), otherwise not (in ghusl). There is a debate about whether using one cup of water is acceptable. The Hanafi school holds that each act should have its own water, and for the three repetitions, new water should be taken each time, contrary to the Shafi'i view. The passage also discusses whether madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah; according to the stronger opinion, they are confirmed sunnahs, and abandoning them without reason is sinful. Evidence from the continuous practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the Companions is presented. The author concludes with a discussion of the hadith of al-Tabarani regarding taking new water for each repetition and the grading of Abu Dawud's silence on a hadith as indicating hasan according to al-Nawawi.

Key Terms
المضمضة (al-madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, terminologically: thorough washing of the entire mouth.
الاستنشاق (al-istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose to the soft part.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; leaving it is disliked and may be sinful, but not as sinful as leaving a wajib.
التثليث (al-tathlith): Performing an act three times.
الاستنثار (al-istinthar): Expelling water from the nose after istinshaq.
الغرغرة (al-ghargarah): Gargling: moving water in the throat to ensure thorough rinsing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of taking new water for each repetition (tathlith) of madmadah and istinshaq?
A) Wajib – the act is invalid without new water.
B) Sunnah – it is recommended but not required.
C) Mustahabb – it is supererogatory with no sin if omitted.
D) Makruh – it is disliked to repeat three times.

Key Takeaway
Madmadah and istinshaq are sunnah mu'akkadah in wudu and ghusl; performing them with fresh water for each act and each repetition follows the Hanafi position based on explicit hadith.
